## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population P and time t, which is the canonical form of population dynamics ODEs. The relationship likely involves density-dependent growth mechanisms such as logistic growth, Allee effects, or variants with time-dependent parameters.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreasing logarithmically with population)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Logistic with Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (strong Allee effect with critical threshold)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (growth with density-dependent birth rate)
- Time-varying logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal carrying capacity or growth rate)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (cubic density dependence)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power growth dynamics)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (constant yield harvesting)
- Logistic with proportional harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (proportional removal)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent negative feedback → quadratic term -c*P^2 appears alongside linear +c*P term (logistic-type self-limitation)
- Allee effect (positive density dependence at low P) → cubic polynomial in P with sign pattern (+P^3 or -P^3 combined with lower-order terms creating an intermediate unstable equilibrium)
- Multiple equilibria in population models → polynomial of degree n in P yields up to n fixed points when dP/dt=0
- Seasonal/periodic forcing in population dynamics → multiplicative sinusoidal modulation sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) on growth rate terms
- Metabolic scaling in growth → fractional powers of P (e.g., P^(2/3) or P^(3/4)) reflecting surface-area-to-volume or metabolic allometry
- Depensation / critical population threshold → factor (P - c) creating a minimum viable population below which dP/dt < 0
- Ratio of polynomials in P → rational density dependence where per-capita rates saturate (Michaelis-Menten-like birth/death rates)
- Logarithmic feedback → log(P) terms indicating Gompertz-type growth where per-capita rate declines logarithmically rather than linearly with P

= 0.1387·P²/8.038 - 0.1387·P³/(8.038·70.018) - 0.1387·P + 0.1387·P²/70.018

**Term 2:** `0.1387*(1 - P/70.018)*P` = 0.1387·P - 0.1387·P²/70.018

**Term 3:** `0.1387*P/(1 + exp(-8.038*(P - 0.5894)))`

## GT Analysis

The GT is:
```
0.13870625668024555*(-1 + P/8.038138014396704)*(1 - P/70.01799944958296)*P + 0.13870625668024555*(1 - P/70.01799944958296)*P + 0.13870625668024555*P/(1 + exp(-8.038138014396704*(-0.5894251550796137 + P)))
```

Let me simplify. Let me denote α = 0.138706..., a = 8.038138..., b = 70.018...

**Term 1:** α*(-1 + P/a)*(1 - P/b)*P
= α*(P/a - 1)*(1 - P/b)*P

**Term 2:** α*(1 - P/b)*P

**Term 3:** α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(-0.5894... + P))) = α*P/(1 + exp(-a*P + a*0.5894...))

Let me expand Terms 1+2:
Term 1 = α*P*(P/a - 1)*(1 - P/b) = α*P*[(P/a)(1-P/b) - (1-P/b)]
= α*P*[P/a - P²/(ab) - 1 + P/b]

Term 2 = α*P*(1 - P/b) = α*P - α*P²/b

Terms 1+2 = α*P*[P/a - P²/(ab) - 1 + P/b] + α*P - α*P²/b
= α*[P²/a - P³/(ab) - P + P²/b + P - P²/b]
= α*[P²/a - P³/(ab)]
= α*P²/a*(1 - P/b)

So GT = α*P²/a*(1 - P/b) + α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(P - 0.5894...)))

Numerically: α/a ≈ 0.01726..., and α/(a*b) ≈ 0.000246...

GT = α*P²/a - α*P³/(ab) + α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(P - 0.5894...)))

This is a **cubic polynomial in P** plus a **sigmoid term** in P. The key basis functions are: P², P³, and P/(1+exp(-a*(P-c))).

The sigmoid term α*P/(1+exp(-a*(P-c))) is a specific nonlinear function. For large P, it approaches α*P; for P near 0, it approaches ~α*P*sigmoid(a*c) ≈ small.

Now let me check each candidate for structural compatibility. The GT has no dependence on `t`, so any candidate with `t` must have those terms zeroed out.

The GT's essential structure is: **cubic in P + sigmoid-weighted P**. The sigmoid P/(1+exp(...)) cannot be represented by polynomials, logs, sines, or simple exponentials.

Let me check candidates that could potentially match:

**Key structural requirements:**
- Must have P³ term (or equivalent)
- Must have P² term
- Must have sigmoid-like term: P/(1+exp(-a*P+...))

Looking through candidates, most use `sin`, `log`, `exp(P*c)` (not sigmoid), or rational functions. None of them contain the sigmoid structure `P/(1+exp(-c*P))`.

The sigmoid `P/(1+exp(-aP+b))` is NOT equivalent to:
- `P*c/(P*c+1)` (rational, different asymptotic behavior)
- `log(c*exp(P*c)+1)` (softplus, not sigmoid*P)
- `exp(P*c)*sin(...)` 
- `sin(log(...))`

Let me verify: Can `c*log(c*exp(P*c)+1)` produce a sigmoid times P? No, softplus ≈ max(0,x), not sigmoid*P.

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain the correct sigmoid structure `P/(1+exp(-a*P))`. The candidates use combinations of polynomials, exponentials, logarithms, trigonometric functions, and rational functions, but none can exactly reproduce the sigmoid term in the GT.
